All Reviews

  1. I don't write many reviews, but thought those wanting to try a straightening kit for the first time might be interested to know about this kit. First off, my hair is very wavy and lightened 2 levels, from light brown to dark blond. It fit the criteria mentioned on the box. It is very fine but is long, very frizzy, and there is lots of it, so from shower to straight takes me 45 minutes with the dryer and flat iron. I don't have hours or hundreds of dollars to spend in the salon, so I figured I've give this kit a shot. I followed the directions exactly. It does have a very strong smell like a perm. Kind of a pain to rinse my hair not once but 3 times through the process. Once I was done my wet hair looked perfectly straight and silky. I was excited! But alas, after blowing it dry it was straight but as frizzy as ever. I used the flat iron, and it did look great for two days. After the requisite two days I washed it again and noticed the waves/curls were less pronounced but again, the frizz remained even after applying the leave-in and allowing it to air dry. I would guess that it will reduce my flat-iron time from around 30 minutes to 20. That's the only real benefit I see from this product. In 3 months I may try a product that is more expensive and is reviewed with better results. So to sum up the pros: slightly reduces wave/curl; makes hair silky soft; retains smoothness and straightness better after flat-ironing; inexpensive To sum up the cons: not a magical frizz eraser, must wait 3 months to touch up (or try a more effective straightener!), only marginally reduces wave. Based on results alone I would only give this 2 stars. You are probably not going to see the results you see on the box. But at $12.99 (at the drugstore) it's worth a shot if you have minimal waves or frizz to tame, so that's why I begrudgingly gave it 3 stars.
  2. Firstly, I came very close to purchasing and experimenting with this product, because I love trying new products. I typically get keratin treatments every 3-4 months (since 2008), and I think they work well with frizzy, coarse, or unruly hair. With that said, to the women who have suffered hair loss or breakage- my heart goes out to you. I have been there before (not with a keratin treatment but with a relaxer). Nioxin hair re-growth system, Phyto, and Rene Furterer are all great products to help strengthen and regrow hair. Phyto and Rene Furterer carry vitamins (with biotin) that will most certainly promote growth. The Nioxin hair system is specifically designed for growth. These products are slightly expensive, but they are well worth the money. Find a good hair stylist to get you through this!<br /><br />Secondly, for those of you who are still interested in getting a keratin treatment, Coppola's Keratin Complex Smoothing Therapy and Kera Straight are my favorite. Ulta Salon offers the Kera Straight treatment, while many salons offer the Coppola treatment. Do your research on the treatment and get a consultation. The keratin treatments typically work well, it's just a matter of finding the right treatment and the right stylist. I hope this helps!

I usually flat iron my hair about every day very lightly as my hair is naturally very straight, but I didn't need to do so this time surprisingly. At first I really wasn't impressed at all as my hair did not look shiny in the least (in fact it looked duller than it usually does), though I noticed my hair felt very soft. Well I washed my hair two days later and instead of blow drying it I let it air dry. My hair looked great! I had to straighten it lightly and after I did so my hair looked so shiny and smooth! Now two weeks later, my hair looks even better than it did after I first used the treatment. The biggest problem I've had with it is it has definitely dried my hair out quite a bit, so I have to use leave-in conditioners to try and restore it, but it doesn't work so well. I don't believe I will use this product again, just because I believe it wasn't so good for my hair, but for a $10 suave product I was fairly impressed.

So for extremely curly hair it says 25 minutes, I only combed it through for 17 minutes. It didn't bring my hair to stick straight, but I didn't want that either. This is also very important for a first time with a product... Easy to say \\"next time i'll keep it on longer\\" much harder to deal with hair fried or falling out. I've done many different processes and honestly I was very pleased with the product. My hair is soft, and actually hangs looser! Yes, it I a perm product, but your hair is not going on rollers... You are doing what they might call a straight perm... Retraining the hair follicles. My suggestion is as the hair dresser said is to do the skin test for irritation and use it for less time. Also the conditioner that comes with the kit is great! You can buy it separately as well... If you are just looking for a smoother, try just buying the shampoo and conditioner instead of the kit!

It smells exactly like a perm, and I'm sure if you curled your hair while doing the treatment, you'd have curly hair. The keratin treatments I've used in the past did not have two steps (like a perm). You put the product on, let it process, dry and straighten. You didn't even rinse it out. This you put on, let it process, rinse, then put in the second product (which stops the \\"perm\\" process) and rinse. A REAL KERATIN treatment (of good quality, like the Copola keratin treatment, which is the one my stylist uses) doesn't need to be done in a well ventalated area because you aren't putting anything harmful on your hair and it smells really good. You CAN do a keratin treatment to damaged hair because the real keratin treatments correct damage to your hair. When you wash you hair after doing a keratin treatment, it feels exactly like you've done NOTHING to your hair. It feels healthy and normal. But when I washed my hair after using this stuff, my hair felt dry and it stuck together really bad. It felt damaged. Naturally, my hair is very thick, very wavy hair. I haven't had any clumps of hair come out, but I have had A LOT of breakage at the ends, so my hair feels very fine and thin in the back. I am going to check with my stylist to see if a real keratin treatment would be helpful in reversing the damage or if I'm just going to have to cut my hair off.   117. I'll start this out by saying that I know, full well, that I'm one of the lucky ones. I have very thick dark hair that, as I've gotten older (and a little grey has made it's way in) has a more dramatic reaction to the humidity than it did when I was younger.<br /><br />I had a Brazilian Keratin treatment at a salon several years ago. And that.. to this day.. stands as the best hair day of my life. Exorbitantly pricey, my hair came out of that looking incredibly fab, feeling fantastic, and I was able to maintain the great style my hair sylist had accomplished.<br /><br />So as I got older and the hairs on the top of my head were a bit more dry and kinked, I moved to deep conditioners and the trusty flat iron. I have been considering getting another treatment to get it under control, because when the humidity is up.. my hair floofs.<br /><br />So I spotted this in the store and for ten bucks? figured why not? Keratin is good for your hair, and so in theory there's no way you can really damage it using Keratin. It should just smooth and weigh down the cuticles and generally make it behave better.<br /><br />I read the instructions; and it didn't seem too out of line with my professional experience. The extra step I figured wasn't a big deal. This is Keratin right?<br /><br />WRONG. Let me tell you now. The Step 1 of this is a perm solution. there is no way around that. There's a logic to it that I get. Just like a perm can be used to force tight curls in hair, it can be used to force them out. But it strips down the hair to accomplish that. (Natural curls in hair are actually due to a variance in thickness in the cuticle of the hair.) So a Perm basically shaves off the outside of the cuticle of your hair.<br /><br />So let me repeat myself here. STEP 1 IS A PERM SOLUTION. If your hair cannot handle a perm, then this is not going to be happy ending for you. If you're not comfortable perming your hair at home; then Step 1 is not going to help that.<br /><br />I'm fortunate in that my hair can handle more than a bit of abuse, I just don't abuse it regularly. And when I smelled Step 1? I decided not to abuse it then either.<br /><br />What I did do? I totally skipped step 1. I went straight for Step 2; and saturated my hair with that much more pleasant smelling cream. Turns out THAT was the actual Keratin. I had an accidental moment of smart. So I let that one soak all in to my wet hair. It actually sat in my hair for about 12 minutes. I rinsed it out; applied the Step 3. I'm happy with the results.<br /><br />The flyaways that are normally at the top of my hair are smooth and flat now. My hair feels great; it lays well with its layers, and so I'm okay with that. I don't know that it's going to last anywhere near as long as the Salon version; nor do I expect it to come anywhere close to the awesome that is the Coppola Keratin treatments. But for ten bucks? I'm not unhappy.<br /><br />That being said. This is nothing like a salon keratin treatment. You ARE adding Perm chemicals to your hair; and hair that doesn't handle those well is going to break; melt, and split..just like what happens when you get a bad home perm.<br /><br />My advice? Skip step 1. Go straight to step 2 and don't risk your coiffure. Maybe it won't last a whole month; but there are other products out there that last longer. This is Suave. It's not meant to be perfect replacement to the pricier products they mimic. (Seriously.. their idea of mimicking Aveda's Rosemary Mint Shampoo and Conditioner is laughable) But you can get good results from it; if you're aware of what's going on.<br /><br />In other words, if you don't want to perm your hair? Skip Step 1. There's no reason for it. (I'm guessing it's included because it should make the treatment last longer)>I'm fortunate in that my hair can handle more than a bit of abuse, I just don't abuse it regularly. Experts then look for reports related to the same product or similar ones. FDA scientists will use the information to determine if the product has a history of problems and represents a public health concern that needs to be addressed.<br /><br />If you file a consumer report, your identity will remain confidential.

(Through experience, I find that air drying my hair a little before blow drying it, a week or so after having it straightened, helps me maintain the straight look longer.) That's why I still rely on other people to do it. After about 10 minutes of applying it thoroughly (maybe slightly more), then 20 minutes of constantly combing and using my hands to flatten the hair repeatedly with some slight massaging and pulling of the hair downwards to keep it straight, I got a crick in my neck and elbows the first time I used this. (I tried to avoid this the 2nd time by stretching my arms above my head after each combing/massaging/pulling action every few minutes.) I think there were some places in the back of my head that I probably missed the first time because for a while my hair looked like there was a small wedge in the back when I looked at my hair sideways. It is time consuming and should not be done the day you're going to a special occasion where you want to wow everyone with your straight hair. I suggest you do it on a weekend or the night before the occasion. I bemoaned the fact that I wasn't able to do some work on my laptop while straightening my hair, which I can do when I go to the salon to have it done. Depending on how you look at it, doing this yourself can save you time and money because you don't have to do it professionally, but for me it sort of cost me the same because I realized how much work I am actually able to do in one hour while someone else straightens my hair for me. I only say this because I have a very demanding job that demands a lot of my time, so I really don't have time to spend straightening my hair myself. This is only a warning to others who may think that it might be easier to do hair straightening yourself than pay someone else to do it. If you have been doing ityourself for years, then you probably have the methods and time down pat, but I haven't done this since I left college, so it's been a long while! That being said, this product saved me one trip to the salon and gave me the same results.
